  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5d0e95dd-5499-45c6-b905-60e99bbf6f8b'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer288385055166143662">How fascinating!! I enjoyed this book. It's a quick read but filled with many fascinating elements like medieval inspiration, magical references, and a political dynamic that made me want to know more about the world. <br/><br/>The characters, however, are what make this book great. Each of them come to life in such a way that I felt connected to them.   <span id="freeText288385055166143662" style="display:none">How fascinating!! I enjoyed this book. It's a quick read but filled with many fascinating elements like medieval inspiration, magical references, and a political dynamic that made me want to know more about the world. <br /><br />The characters, however, are what make this book great. Each of them come to life in such a way that I felt connected to them. They had their own personalities that came across well, especially from the main characters who I absolutely loved. <br /><br />As for the plot, I liked how it was relatively straightforward. There was a dark element to the plot too, which prevented the story from becoming a cheesy love story. <br /><br />And then there is the ending... I wanted to cry! Why! Why! Why! But overall, it was a thrilling read and one that certainly made me want to get the follow-up!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11196031658900254761">I absolutely loved this book!! This was great storytelling as it was in The Evening Tide! <br/><br/>Young love, elves, and an incredibly fascinating world, with a shocking ending, comes out of nowhere. <br/><br/>I love these characters; Teegs was so funny, Jaydan was so charming.   <span id="freeText11196031658900254761" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this book!! This was great storytelling as it was in The Evening Tide! <br /><br />Young love, elves, and an incredibly fascinating world, with a shocking ending, comes out of nowhere. <br /><br />I love these characters; Teegs was so funny, Jaydan was so charming. Stase is complex, and I envision a beautiful and sweet elvess but strong and stubborn, very independent! <br /><br />My heart goes out to Stase! Without giving anything away, I feel like I understand her dilemma in choosing between love with Jay and her deep desire to be 'free' and travel! Beautifully done! I loved the dynamic that these three, along with Lardian, Teegs, Nendia, and Alardia, gave to this story. <br /><br />These six friends find themselves attending the Karnaea for a great time but are thrust into a world suddenly fearful when the Old Way is discovered to be in the city! <br /><br />I loved everything about this book; Characters, world-building, romance, the mistrust, the dark atmosphere that slowly settles somewhere halfway. I loved the elements of humor too. Then, of course, the twist at the end shook me! <br /><br />I have already bought The Missing, and I am itching to find out what happens in this next installment!</span>

<div id="review_2422614229" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2422614229" />
    <a title="Jess (DYHMD)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82730230-jess-dyhmd"><img alt="Jess (DYHMD)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556442705p2/82730230.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2422614229?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess (DYHMD)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess (DYHMD)" href="/user/show/82730230-jess-dyhmd">Jess (DYHMD)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2422614229" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1971945646399039314">I loved this and while thinking about what to say in this review, I found it hard to define why this book really resonated with me!!<br/><br/>The obvious appeal came from the story itself; it is interesting, the plot was well thought out. The world as well was very fascinating, the cultures that I discovered, were intriguing and I really liked how there were subtle tie-ins with The Evening Tide!<br/><br/>The characters were well written too and to be honest, I think that is it; they were so believable, so real. I f</span>
  <span id="freeText1971945646399039314" style="display:none">I loved this and while thinking about what to say in this review, I found it hard to define why this book really resonated with me!!<br /><br />The obvious appeal came from the story itself; it is interesting, the plot was well thought out. The world as well was very fascinating, the cultures that I discovered, were intriguing and I really liked how there were subtle tie-ins with The Evening Tide!<br /><br />The characters were well written too and to be honest, I think that is it; they were so believable, so real. I felt connected to them in some weird way. I found Teegs funny. I found Jay charming but above all, I related to Stace so much and that is what I look for in books; to feel the characters, to understand them. <br /><br />The way this book ended really made me think but not just that, it made me feel too. I understand Stace's feelings, I get why she had so many reservations and fear. I don't know. I just feel like I get her and I wish the story continued, I wish I got to have some idea as to what happened to her. I actually feel like crying. I feel like I formed this connection only to have it snatched away without understanding why! If she had died, fine! I get it, life happens but the ambiguous way Stace's story ended, left me not knowing what happened to her and that is what frustrates me, makes me feel as if somehow, this book cheated me. Because of that, I felt like giving this book 3 stars but couldn't, for it really is a good book. The reviewers were right; its quick and easy to read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1971945646399039314" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2418482352?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="SonOfYork" class="user" itemprop="url" name="SonOfYork" href="/user/show/82688455-sonofyork">SonOfYork</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/82688455-sonofyork?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2418482352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer900262086824788709">After reading The Evening Tide, my expectation was to begin its sequel; instead, I found that The Broken Rose is more of a crossover, a stand-alone with minor and subtle tie-ins to its predecessor. None the less, I enjoyed the read. It's quick and direct with very engaging characters. <br/><br/>The Moon Elves in contrast to the Sun Elves, appear to have more depth, live in a functioning society with its own unique culture and law. The way the author brought these elements across was brilliant and I especi</span>
  <span id="freeText900262086824788709" style="display:none">After reading The Evening Tide, my expectation was to begin its sequel; instead, I found that The Broken Rose is more of a crossover, a stand-alone with minor and subtle tie-ins to its predecessor. None the less, I enjoyed the read. It's quick and direct with very engaging characters. <br /><br />The Moon Elves in contrast to the Sun Elves, appear to have more depth, live in a functioning society with its own unique culture and law. The way the author brought these elements across was brilliant and I especially enjoyed the similarities that this new world has to our own medieval England. Also, I was pleased to find that Asharal (The Evening Tide's main character) had a brief cameo and that despite the years that have passed between the events of The Evening Tide and that of The Broken Rose, his imposing and illustrious flare remains intact. He is still the badass we all remember him to be!<br /><br />For readers who love fantasy and elves, who enjoy a good and quick read and who are drawn to romances, this is a book you'll find quite refreshing.</span>
  <a data-text-id="900262086824788709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2592914838" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2592914838" />
    <a title="Joc" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68172472-joc"><img alt="Joc" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537103104p2/68172472.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2592914838?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joc" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joc" href="/user/show/68172472-joc">Joc</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38097695-the-broken-rose">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68172472-joc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2592914838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16907272713471649429">Although set in the same Elven world as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35164507-the-evening-tide' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Evening Tide</a>, this is a stand-alone fantasy novel with only minor crossover elements. Moon Elves are converging on Asher City where victory celebrations will be held in the form of the Karnaea tournaments. Elder Dayane has successfully pushed back the Sun Elves establishing Moon dominance in the realm.<br/><br/>Stasanda has joined the queue of elves wanting to gain entry to Asher City but there is a ripple of concern running through the prospective tournament go</span>
  <span id="freeText16907272713471649429" style="display:none">Although set in the same Elven world as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35164507-the-evening-tide" rel="nofollow noopener">The Evening Tide</a>, this is a stand-alone fantasy novel with only minor crossover elements. Moon Elves are converging on Asher City where victory celebrations will be held in the form of the Karnaea tournaments. Elder Dayane has successfully pushed back the Sun Elves establishing Moon dominance in the realm.<br /><br />Stasanda has joined the queue of elves wanting to gain entry to Asher City but there is a ripple of concern running through the prospective tournament goers. The sentinels are checking for Dead God worshippers and preventing their entry into the city. Stasanda doesn’t think she needs to be concerned. In another area, Jaydan and his friends, Tegerian and Lardian, are also seeking entry to the city but not in the conventional way.<br /><br />For most of the novel, the story is told from the alternating points of view of Stasanda and Jaydan in first person. They want to trust each other but there is a small element of doubt arising which gives a nice tension to their interactions and also amongst their respective friends. That said, however, there was an underlying tension relating to the continued searching for Dead God worshippers that I felt wasn’t as sinister or constant as it could have been which meant I felt the pace lagging a little in the middle.<br /><br />I found I wasn’t as engaged with Stasanda and Jaydan as I could have been. The secondary characters of Alardia and Tegerian held more of my interest. I enjoyed the world building and I enjoyed the read but not as much as I enjoyed <i>The Evening Tide.</i> My rating is sitting at three and half stars, rounded up.<br /><br /><i>Book received from the author for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="16907272713471649429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

Bring on the next one!</span>

<div id="review_2703403128" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2703403128" />
    <a title="Mak" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66553282-mak"><img alt="Mak" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546523711p2/66553282.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2703403128?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mak" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mak" href="/user/show/66553282-mak">Mak</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66553282-mak?shelf=smss">smss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer2703403128&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2703403128" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4943772141724653408">Read it a second time and still my heart shattered again in million pieces. This is my favourite book in the Sun, Moon, Sand and Star series and it always affects me deeply. Another sleepless night pondering the whys and the hows. But, I guess that's the beauty of it; you never know how things will turn out, how and it will escalate and that happily ever after is perhaps happily ever moment!<br/><br/>**<br/>Huh! I was not fooled this time! I read this in one sitting, as I should had done with The Evening Tide </span>
  <span id="freeText4943772141724653408" style="display:none">Read it a second time and still my heart shattered again in million pieces. This is my favourite book in the Sun, Moon, Sand and Star series and it always affects me deeply. Another sleepless night pondering the whys and the hows. But, I guess that's the beauty of it; you never know how things will turn out, how and it will escalate and that happily ever after is perhaps happily ever moment!<br /><br />**<br />Huh! I was not fooled this time! I read this in one sitting, as I should had done with The Evening Tide as well. <br /><br />This book is also short, but it is packed with a combination of elements that satisfy the greedy eyes and the thirsty minds of the readers. <br /><br />The whole setting reminded of the Middle Ages and had a slight modern vibe into it. The writing, the dialogues, the manners, were all so Medieval British-proper with a New World-twist. Using the term ‘buddy’ was absolutely entertaining and smart. It is amazing how such small details can make a book stand out. <br /><br />I thoroughly enjoyed the characters and how they were multi-layered, showing so many different aspects. I thought, at first, I minded the lack of their background, but along the way I found myself not really caring, as I was sucked into the story and was fascinated by the series of events. <br /><br />The way the author has weaved romance and mystery into the story is unbelievable. Stasanda is an adventurous Elvess, who has a good sense of humor, who is kind and who values friendship. <br />Jaydan is charming, bold and straight-forward. His infatuation with Stase grows into love with -dare I say- a little bit of obsession in it. There was a mystery surrounding his origins and upon revealing some of it towards the end, I found myself wanting to know more. <br /><br />In the Evening Tide, I was frustrated by the rather cruel ending, and the Broken Rose shares a similar sadness, but I have come to appreciate the author’s unusual approach and I can hardly wait to see if all these loose ends will be bind one day. <br /><br />The last scene with Stasanda in her bedroom was cut abruptly and the details are never given to the reader. I wish we had had a better glimpse of what went down, but I guess this was the author’s way of keeping the mystery and the drama alive. Also, the fact that the author has once again described a near-rape scene had me thinking.<br /><br />The narration in first person, as always, was excellent, and I just loved the epilogue said through the eyes of the Blademaster. To be honest, I kept thinking that the Blademaster would turn out to be something more than just that. The cloud of mystery and menace that surrounded him throughout the book was finally dissolved and I was surprised to see someone underneath who feels compassion and guilt. <br /><br />As for the fabled rivals of the Moon Elves, the Sun Elves and their notorious Father of the Sun, this was a subtle, yet brilliant way of connecting the two realms. The Moon Elves seem to have a richer culture and are driven by religious beliefs. They have a rich history and they rely strongly on their Elder and the blademasters and feel blessed by the grace of the Whispering god. Whereas, the Sun elves seem to be a more closed society, darker, and with great gaps between elves and elvesses, as well as social status. <br /><br />Also, it is pointed out how the Father of the Sun is not worshipped by all the Elves in his realm, but only by those who he shows preference towards; once again referring to Asharal’s arrogance and cruelty. The Blademaster's memory of his encounter with Asharal was one of the best parts!<br /><br /><i> “Know this Moon Elf. Though the Moon has overcome the Sun, the Highborns are eternal and are therefore, content to wait," his pale eyes piercing my soul. “Enjoy these islands whilst you still live, Blademaster. When I hear that death has claimed you, the fight for the Middle Islands will begin again.” </i><br /><br />There are so many things I would love to know more about: the war between the Moon Elves and the Sun Elves with more facts and details, the encounter between the Blademaster and Asharal, what happened to Stasanda, what did Jay’s letter say, why Lardian followed the old gods, what was Asharal’s warning to the Blademaster, the signs of Adonai, will we ever learn more about the Blue Elves or the Gatheians, and so many more. <br /><br />It seems that, the more I write the more I want to say, but I don’t want to tire anyone with my bazilion thoughts. <br /><br />Once again, I would like to congratulate Jeremy Forsyth, for thinking out of the box and for offering a unique reading experience. Indeed, I agree that a giant of fantasy has emerged out of South Africa!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4943772141724653408" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Edward" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87400615-edward"><img alt="Edward" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1538210725p2/87400615.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2553290741?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward" href="/user/show/87400615-edward">Edward</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2553290741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2507192286330922489">A great story!<br/><br/>I now prefer the Moon Elves to the Sun Elves and was impressed by this book's ability to make me switch sides just two chapters in. <br/><br/>This is a very endearing love story about two young Moon Elves and their friends, who wish to attend the Karnaea, (a somewhat elf version of a medieval tournament). There is a level of mistrust that slowly seeps its way into the group which kept me wondering throughout each chapter. I liked that! <br/><br/>As I found in The Evening Tide, the characters were writ</span>
  <span id="freeText2507192286330922489" style="display:none">A great story!<br /><br />I now prefer the Moon Elves to the Sun Elves and was impressed by this book's ability to make me switch sides just two chapters in. <br /><br />This is a very endearing love story about two young Moon Elves and their friends, who wish to attend the Karnaea, (a somewhat elf version of a medieval tournament). There is a level of mistrust that slowly seeps its way into the group which kept me wondering throughout each chapter. I liked that! <br /><br />As I found in The Evening Tide, the characters were written really well, each invoking a unique flair that added to the dynamic of the story, not one of them being bland or what I like to call, a 'space filler', which is something I have noticed in fantasy these days; a character is introduced who does not add or detract from the story but simply is there. I hate that! <br /><br />The Moon Elves seem to have a rich culture, religious conflicts, and secret societies, as well as elite warriors in the form of blademasters! I want to know more about the Destroyer and the rest of his blademaster brethren. <br /><br />I also appreciate how such a small book was able to encompass all the above without drifting away from the main story. That's a sign of a real storyteller!! <br /><br />Lastly, the ending was great, shocking and a bit sad but otherwise, a well-done conclusion. I hope to find some resolution in the third installment but I get the feeling that the author enjoys leaving lots of mystery around his stories and so I will just have to see.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2507192286330922489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Teegs was a cool character; he made me chuckle more often than not while Nendia was pleasantly dislikable. Alardia was cool too but not as distinctive as the other characters. Jay seemed like a bit of a sucker but the love between him and Stasanda was interesting and the ending was done really well. <br/><br/>I like these elves, I like this world. 5 stars!</span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/38097695-the-broken-rose">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61573845-lou?shelf=supporting-indie-authors">supporting-indie-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61573845-lou?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61573845-lou?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2521924022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4497277310150837835"><i>I was given a free pdf copy from the author. This in no way sways my opinion of the book.</i><br/><br/><i>3.5 stars</i><br/>Consider me shook. I wasn't expecting to like this as much as I did! The book itself is really short (about 60 or something pages depending on the edition) but there's so much world-building in there it's hard to believe looking back it is that short! I'm in awe at how good the world-building is, it's definitely made me think on how I can make my NaNoWriMo draft better. The writing (besides the worl</span>
  <span id="freeText4497277310150837835" style="display:none"><i>I was given a free pdf copy from the author. This in no way sways my opinion of the book.</i><br /><br /><i>3.5 stars</i><br />Consider me shook. I wasn't expecting to like this as much as I did! The book itself is really short (about 60 or something pages depending on the edition) but there's so much world-building in there it's hard to believe looking back it is that short! I'm in awe at how good the world-building is, it's definitely made me think on how I can make my NaNoWriMo draft better. The writing (besides the world) was my favourite part, it was so good! I could reread this over and over just for the writing (and the world).<br />On the negative side of things, there's insta-love. It's understandable since the book's so short, things are bound to go fast. But sometimes I couldn't help thinking... why does Jaydan love this elvess so much? Their first meeting didn't give off any indication that he was going to fall for her then straight after, he does. The ending had me a bit confused as well. <br />But besides from these minor problems I had with it, I altogether had a brill time reading. It's one of those books where you're gonna need tissues while reading the ending, trust me.<br /><br /><i>TW: attempted rape</i></span>

<div id="review_2419226907" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Nikita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/82926209-nikita"><img alt="Nikita" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2419226907?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nikita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nikita" href="/user/show/82926209-nikita">Nikita</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2419226907" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7512245759013487229">Although I loved the action of The Evening Tide, I was thoroughly captivated by the love story that Jeremy twisted into the threads of a world struggling through religious and political upheaval; all encompassed in a universe that your heart will long to visit! The characters are captivating and no one sets a scene quite like Jeremy. The book will leave you with moments that will still be crystal clear in your mind for years to come! </span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2745322494" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13503527308263481330">3.5. I found this book more straight-forward and easier to follow than <i>The Evening Tide</i>— at least until I got to the ending. I reread the last chapter and the epilogue a couple of times to try to understand what had happened. Not 100% sure. I’d love more clarity on that. <br/><br/>While not a big fan of insta-love, I did appreciate the Jay-Stase arc and the use of it to frame the conflict between those allegiant to Adonia and those allegiant to the Old Way. I must admit I was rooting for Jay. <br/><br/>There are se</span>
  <span id="freeText13503527308263481330" style="display:none">3.5. I found this book more straight-forward and easier to follow than <i>The Evening Tide</i>— at least until I got to the ending. I reread the last chapter and the epilogue a couple of times to try to understand what had happened. Not 100% sure. I’d love more clarity on that. <br /><br />While not a big fan of insta-love, I did appreciate the Jay-Stase arc and the use of it to frame the conflict between those allegiant to Adonia and those allegiant to the Old Way. I must admit I was rooting for Jay. <br /><br />There are several interesting characters. I wish they were more fleshed out. Alardia, for example. Good or bad? She did something that seems bad, but I need more information to decide. Perhaps due to the shortness of the book, ambiguity about their characters remains unresolved. <br /><br />Thanks to Jeremy for proving me with a free copy in exchange for my thoughts. Seems like you have a keen imagination and lots of original ideas. Keep writing! </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14255285511029946424">I loved The Evening Tide but The Broken Rose is now my favorite! <br/><br/>The two main characters were not long in endearing themselves to me and the world that the author has created is very intriguing. <br/><br/>The ending did leave me feeling a bit sad but due to the clever twists that I have come to expect at the end of the author’s works, I am ready and eager for the next one!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText12981581177214204060" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549092484ra/27004106.gif" width="500" height="499" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549092861ra/27004122.gif" width="500" height="499" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549093100ra/27004135.gif" width="500" height="499" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549093212ra/27004138.gif" height="499" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1549093366ra/27004143.gif" height="499" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549093494i/27004149._SX540_.png" height="499" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This story has many possibilities, and many possible meanings. When you look at the meaning of the white rose it <br>suggests a symbol of honor, reverence secrecy ,worthiness, innocence , and purity. The readers finds all of these symbols throughout <br>the entire story. Visions and Prophecy are key elements, and play major roles in this story.<br>When you read the story you find an innocent maid removed from the city -- and it appears that she is dismissed for practicing<br>the Old Ways-- but in truth she was removed for her own safety, due to a vision that fore warned of <br>impending danger to her if she remained. The white rose symbolizes secrecy. <br>Things aren't always what they seem. As is the case with Jay and his friend Lardian. The white rose<br>symbolizes honor and reverence. <br>This could also show us the reasoning of secrecy of the Old Ways.<br>The author said it best," Elves who had still held fast to the old gods have waged a secret and eternal war against believers<br> of Adonai ever since - the Silent War,<br> It dated back to the Great Split during<br> the First Moon - when the First Elder declared Adonai the one true God of the Moon Elves.<br> He had ordered the images and idols of the old gods to be burned.<br>This has a lot to do with the divisions of the elves and why they hated each other.<br>Currently the Moon Elves are ruling the land -- but a vision to the Blade Master warns him <br> the Father of the Sun; the Highborn immortal, Asharal Evening The Father of the Sun looked at me. “Know this Moon Elf.<br> Though the Moon has overcome the Sun, the Highborn s are eternal and are therefore, content to wait," his pale eyes piercing my soul. <br>The utter contempt I had perceived in them, I could recall, had been extremely unsettling. <br> When I hear that death has claimed you, the fight for the Middle Islands will begin again.” <br>In the mean time the remaining Old Way followers remain in secret, and will kill as many of the Moon Elves as possible.<br>So our story continues.... A Very Excellent read !!! I love the many layers this story has --<br><br><br><br><br><br><br></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yGSIVqhKXqKTVmzmbIVdcMLfc2Ntr5GtnUf7VaEnMRLSi7wgUnpnUXI5JRlSE6ME8Uqs4xL+rSfi0IIo2umDHw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_55701105').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_55701105').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_55701105').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
